Nah... just nah....
I can see this game has good intentions, the theory behind it is sound. But the execution of it falls short and makes it come across as, awkward?

My test Gameplay:
https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=F2d9uo4E6kE&lc=z13rjr4o2wbmc33to23fvxvxrmegwvkjg04

I love the idea of it all. But even without the long all too frequent loading times, the graphical bugs and errors, the painful voice acting that can clearly be heard as one man changing his accents. Its just not right?

Characters fleet in and out of nowhere, random events happen at the start with too little going on and all spread out with awfully timed loading screens. Things that just would never happen... happen. It just breaks down the immersion and causes laughter rather than gripping emotion.

METAPHORIC SUMMARY

Its kind of like a beautiful girl you know is amazing and perfect. But when you go out on a date with her, all her makeup is overdone, she is wearing hot-pants and fishnets to a evening dinner down the local Chinese and she stinks of cheap booze and ciggies... Shes lovely... but shes just not right? As much as you want to get to the end game (wink wink), you cant wait to just drop her off and stop feeling awkward :(

Ã‰valuation publiÃ©e le 28 juillet 2016
Produit reÃ§u gratuitement

I can't recommend this simply because of the price. I was expecting hours of gameplay and only got a few. I was given this as a gift, but would have rathered received a more worthy game.

You're set in a French courtroom where you as a defendent must defend yourself by coming up with evidence/excuses to excuse yourself of murder.

The game is really good, and you walkthrough your testimony. It lacks though in chioces; it says your choices will change your fate, but by how much? Really, there's no dialogue choices, just actions only. This game is onto something really good, but isn't quite there. It has a really good simulation part, but it seems to be made part way. After your first case is done with a few hours in there's no other cases. This has very little replay value as well.

If they would either add more cases, or add more replay value I would definetly upvote this. But please save your money. If you played the Deed it's similar to that concept only 3-D and way more costly.

Ã‰valuation publiÃ©e le 31 mars 2017
Produit reÃ§u gratuitement

Just got this as a review key ( for beta testing on the newly added controller support)
My views on this game aren't affected by getting a copy for free~

To start, I really dig this concept : you are essentially re-telling past events through gameplay in an effort to clear your name of murder.

IM not even sure if you did the murder or not.. the writing is pretty well done, and is very rich in French culture and events.
I love the art style, its very pleasing to the eye.

The controller support works fine enough, but the analogue stick controlling the camera is slightly stiff, as it gets stuck when you move up or down, only if you keep it held in a direction and try to switch it rapidly. Releasing the analogue stick returns control to you . A bit stiff, but this is the reason why they issue out keys to beta test!

Overall, I enjoyed my first run and getting to experience the world through Ethon's eyes. I will have to delve deeper into this to fully understand the concepts and mechanics, as i was absolutley found guilty and lost my head lol.

I recommend this to anyone that enjoys old films and mysteries involving wrongfully accused murderers, or murderers that get away with it !

Ã‰valuation publiÃ©e le 19 dÃ©cembre 2023
Try to get it on offer, but for ten pounds I would say this game is well worth it.

Many of the mechanics are janky, and I had a hard time figuring out what I'm supposed to be doing when I first played it. But after many hours with it, I enjoyed teasing out the story from the information given, and playing around with all the freedom the game gives you to do what you want.

The concept is brilliant, the execution is uneven. But I think the concept is strong enough that it shines through and makes this game a lot of fun, even when it's confusing or clunky. I also really enjoy the French accents on display, but your mileage may vary there.

I'd recommend picking this game up and being patient with it. Expect to be confused at first. Once you've figured out what the actual crime is, you can then start weaving your lies and planning the story you want to tell. Maybe, for your first playthrough, aim for a confession. I would advise not resorting to guides unless you have to, but there are many good ones that may help you get through something confusing or janky so that you can continue to enjoy playing around with the game. For Â£9.99, I would say go for it. I had a lot of fun and hopefully you will too.

2.2 h en tout
Ã‰valuation publiÃ©e le 21 fÃ©vrier 2022
Bohemian Killing is unlike any other crime/detective/courtroom game I've ever played - I daresay this is a genre-defining game. In this game, you've been arrested for murdering a woman and you're now giving testimony in your court case. The way you provide your testimony is by replaying the events of the night in question. You're given a rough timeline of the events of the evening, so in order for the judge to find your testimony truthful, you need to make sure your actions at those times are corroborated by the evidence.

Bohemian Killing is a really interesting game, but its lack of polish makes it difficult for me to recommend it to other players. With more work (and more content), this game has potential akin to The Return of the Obra Dinn and The Last Express. What I would really like to see is another game of this genre, but more fleshed out and with fewer bugs.
 
Palchan

Ã‰valuation publiÃ©e le 18 dÃ©cembre 2020
As many others said already, interesting concept but poorly executed. First playthrough throws you straight into unfolding events without enough guidance nor explanation, and quickly becomes a 'bad ending' by design, without teaching you anything new about game mechanics or anything. What was supposed to be a 'trial and error' approach, as a tedious substitution for a proper tutorial, turns out to be a massive waste of time for the player, forced to re-live situations in the mere hope that some correct random interaction with world objects will trigger some positive chain of events and therefore a positive outcome. There isn't really enough room to build a solid defense the way you'd like to, because the game will allow only a pre-determined set of combinations - regarding what happens in your given time and space - to be 'win material' for your cause. Not to mention the tediousness of trying again and again until you find - more by chance or exhaustion of possibilities rather than thanks to logic - one of those combinations. As a result, it feels like playing a very linear puzzle-game, but in the most confusing way possible.

5 (for the effort, and the good concept) out of 10

Music and art style are nice, voice acting is good too. The game has its quirks, especially around picking up and placing the knife down, but ultimately it's very enjoyable.

Ã‰valuation publiÃ©e le 14 mai 2020
It has some flaws but overall is an interesting take on the murder genre. Are you the actual killer? Are you being framed? Are you a liar or are you crazy? Your actions get to determine that outcome in a neat sort of puzzle/time management way.

There are an impressive amount of different paths you can take to prove your innocence...or guilt.

6.9 h en tout
Ã‰valuation publiÃ©e le 27 mars 2019
This is quite a clever game, where you play a murderer attempting to justify his crimes and create reasonable doubt. It accomplishes this well, using logical puzzles for the most part. The art isn't always the best -- the judge's eyes regularly disappear when he is talking to you, which might just be a very effective method of intimidating a defendant. There are multiple endings, which makes for nice replayability, and the author helpfully provided a guide to help players get to some of the more obscure ones. Excellent work! I look forward to more from this developer!

Ã‰valuation publiÃ©e le 10 aout 2018
Nice game.
I've played detective games but not help-murderer-get-away games, it's creative.
Basically it's a walking simulation in two of 3-floor-building to look for evidence to make the murderer innocent. It has some logic but more should be given because in most case you can't predict what is going to happen, there' might be no trail to follow and all you do is follow your feeling before your lawyer or the judge revail the connection between your findings and the case. The multi ending is good, but would be better if save slots were given.

Main merit is the court scene defend when near end both prosecutor and defendant lawyer gives speeches. Also I like the voice actor guy, even this dude voiced the player, and the player's mom.
